The author of this book, having completed for you, my sons, this book which is a part of the complete science of medicine and reached its limit in clarity and explanation, saw fit to complete it with this discourse which is a part of practical work with the hand.
Because practical work with the hand has entirely disappeared in our country and in our time, to the point that the science of it is nearly forgotten and its practice has ceased. And only a few illustrations of it remain in the books of our predecessors, which hands have corrupted, error and confusion have befallen, to the point that their meanings are obscured and their benefits are distant.
So I decided to revive it and compose this discourse in a way that explains, clarifies, and abbreviates. I will also provide illustrations of cautery instruments and other tools needed for work, as this increases clarity and aids what is necessary.
And the reason there is no skilled craftsman in our time who can do this with his hands, is that the practice of medicine is extensive and its practitioner should first engage himself in the study of anatomy, which Galen has described. Until he understands the benefits, forms, temperaments, connections, and disconnections of the organs, as well as the knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their numbers, origins, arteries, veins, and the locations of their origins.
Therefore, Avicenna said that there are many doctors in name but few in reality, especially in the practice of the hand. We have mentioned some of this in the introduction of this book.
Because one who is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned regarding anatomy may fall into errors that can kill people, as I have often witnessed with those who imagine themselves to be experts in this science without knowledge or understanding.
This is because I saw an ignorant doctor who cut into a pig-like tumor on a woman's neck, thereby cutting some of the neck arteries and causing the woman to bleed to death before him.
I also saw another doctor who attempted to remove a stone from a man with bladder problems, and the stone was large. He rushed and removed it along with a piece of the bladder wall. The man died after about three days, and I was called to remove the stone. I saw from the condition of the stone and the state of the patient what had led to that outcome.
I also saw another doctor who earned his living by practicing medicine at the patronage of some patrons in our city.
A young black boy who was under his care had a fracture in his leg near the heel, along with a wound. The doctor, out of his ignorance, quickly applied the splints and bandages too tightly over the fracture and the wound, not leaving any space for the wound to breathe.
Then he let the boy go and indulge in his desires, leaving him for days without releasing the bandages. As a result, the boy's leg and foot swelled, and he was on the brink of death.
I was called to attend to him, and I quickly loosened the bandages. The boy gained some relief and alleviation from his pain, but the damage had already become severe in the affected part, and I could not reverse it.
The damage continued to spread in the affected part until he died.
I also saw another doctor who lanced a malignant tumor, and it became ulcerated after several days, leading to severe suffering for the patient. This is because when cancer is of a pure black type, it should never be treated with an iron instrument at all.
except that it is in a part that can be entirely excised.
Therefore, my son, you should know that work done with the hand is divided into two kinds: work that goes along with safety and work that usually results in damage.
I have warned in every place in this book where there is risk and danger; therefore, you should avoid and reject it.
So that the ignorant cannot find a way to speak and criticize, take caution and care for yourselves, and treat your patients with kindness and certainty.
Use the best method that leads to safety and a commendable outcome, and avoid dangerous and difficult-to-cure diseases.
Abstain from what you fear might cast doubt upon your religion and worldly affairs, for it is safer for your reputation and higher in both this world and the next for your destinies.
Galen said in some of his advices: Do not treat a bad disease and thus become known as bad doctors.
I have divided this article into three sections.
The First Chapter.
On cauterization with fire and sharp medicines, categorized and organized from the head to the foot, including illustrations of instruments, tools for cauterization, and everything needed in manual work.
The Second Chapter.
On incision, closing wounds, bloodletting, cupping, surgeries, extracting arrows, and similar procedures, all categorized and organized with illustrations of instruments.
The Third Chapter.
On bone setting, reduction of dislocations, treatment of wounds, and similar topics, categorized and organized from the finger to the toe, with illustrations of instruments.
The First Chapter.
On cauterization.
And before mentioning how to use it, it is necessary to mention its benefits and harms and in which temperament it is used.
I say that the discussion about the manner in which cauterization is beneficial and harmful is a lengthy discourse, a precise science, and a hidden secret. Many sages have spoken about it.
They disagreed on this matter, and I have briefly summarized their discussions to avoid prolonging the text.
I say that cauterization is generally beneficial for all bad temperaments that occur with matter and without matter, except for two temperaments: the hot temperament without matter and the dry temperament without matter.
As for the dry temperament with matter, they disagreed on it. Some say that cauterization is beneficial in this case, while others argue the opposite, stating that cauterization is not suitable for a disease caused by heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
It is impossible to be cured from a hot and dry disease with a hot and dry treatment. The one who argues the opposite says that cauterization with fire may benefit a hot and dry disease that occurs in people's bodies. Because when you add the body of a human and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you affect the human body with cold.
And I agree with his statement because experience has revealed this to me many times, though it should only be conceived by those who have extensively trained and gained expertise in the art of cauterization. And he observed the differences in the temperaments of people and the conditions of diseases in themselves, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
As for the other temperaments, there is no fear from them, especially for cold and moist diseases, as all physicians have agreed upon them and have not differed regarding the benefit of cauterization in treating them.
Know, my children, that the secret of treating with cauterization by fire and its superiority over medicinal cauterization is that fire is a single essence whose effect does not spread to other organs; it only affects the part that is cauterized, causing minimal harm to adjacent parts.
Cauterization by a burning medicine may extend its effect to subsequent organs, and it might cause a disease in the organ that is difficult to treat or even lead to death. Fire, due to its nobility and noble essence, does not do this unless it is excessive.
This has become clear to us through experience gained from long service, careful attention to the craft, and observing the realities of the matter.
For this reason, I have spared myself the lengthy discourse. However, if it were befitting for my book, I would have presented to you a hidden secret about fire and its effect on bodies in philosophical and demonstrative language, which might exceed your understanding.
And know, my sons, that they have disagreed about the time suitable for cauterization and have considered the springtime to be the best period.
And I say that cauterization may be suitable at any time, because the harm caused by the time is outweighed by the benefit gained from cauterization. Especially if the cauterization is for essential and severe pains that cannot be postponed, due to the fear of consequences that could be worse than the minor harm caused by the time.
And do not let it occur to your minds, my sons, what the common people and ignorant physicians imagine: that cauterization which cures a disease from which there is no return will become a permanent blemish.
And it is not as they suppose, for cauterization is like a medicine that alters the temperament and dries up the humors which are the cause of pains.
However, cauterization is preferable to medicine in the speed of its success, the strength of its effect, and the power of its influence.
And it is possible for the disease to recur at some time depending on the patient's temperament, the persistence and strength of the disease, and what accumulates in his body from excesses and neglect in acquiring necessary nutrients and similar causes.
Except when the disease for which cauterization is used is a mild one in an organ with little excess moisture and humors. Like extracting a tooth for pain and the like, it may be that the pain does not return, and this is rare.
And as for the common belief that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, this statement is correct, not what they themselves believe, because they think that no treatment will be effective with medication or otherwise after the occurrence of cauterization, whereas the matter is contrary to this.
And the meaning of "cauterization is the last resort of medicine" is that whenever we have used various methods of treatment for a disease and those medications were ineffective, then we use cauterization as the final method which may be effective. Therefore, it is said that cauterization is the last resort of medicine. Not in the meaning that the general public and many ignorant physicians have adopted.
I mentioned earlier that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they said this because of the moderation of gold and the nobility of its essence. They also said that the place where gold is used for cauterization does not become ulcerated, but this is not always the case.
Because I have experimented with that and found that it only happens in some bodies and not others. Cauterization with gold is indeed better and preferable to iron, as they said, except that when you heat the cauterizing tool from gold in fire, you cannot tell when it has reached the desired temperature by its color.
And because it quickly cools down, and if you increase its heat in fever, it melts in the fire and spills over, causing the practitioner to be distracted by this. Therefore, cauterization with iron has become faster and closer to accuracy for practical use, God willing.
I have arranged this chapter on cauterization into sections, organizing them from the head to the foot so that it may be easy for the student to find what he desires, God willing.
The first chapter.
On cauterizing the head with one cauterization.
This cauterization is beneficial for the dominance of humidity and coldness over the brain, which are causes of headache, frequent discharges from the head towards the eyes and ears, excessive sleep, tooth pain, and throat pains. In general, it is beneficial for all diseases caused by coldness such as paralysis, epilepsy, syncope, and similar ailments.
The method of this cauterization is that the patient should first be ordered to vomit with a purgative and cleansing medicine for three nights or four, depending on the strength, age, and habits of the patient.
Then order him to shave his head with scissors, and then seat him in front of you in a squatting position with his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his eyes, and where your middle finger ends, mark that spot with ink.
Then heat the olive oil cauterization instrument, which has this appearance.
Reveal the bone to the size of a chickpea or a mustard seed, and if you have raised your hand too soon, repeat with the same instrument or another one if it has cooled. Until you see the bone as I have described to you, then take some salt and dissolve it in water. Soak a piece of cotton in it and place it on the spot and leave it for three days.
Then apply a piece of cotton soaked in fat on it and leave it until the redness from the inflammation subsides. Then treat it with the quadruple ointment until it heals, if God wills.
They say that a wound, when left open, extends the pus and is better and more beneficial.
Some have mentioned that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should remain in place until part of the thickness of the bone is burned. Then remove what has been burned from the bone afterward and treat it.
Others say that cauterization should be excessive until it affects the bone strongly, causing small pieces to fall off like a kernel or a small bowl. They claim that this allows steam from the head to dissipate and leaves the wound open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it heals. I do not see these two types of cauterization at all except in some people, and using them is risky; leaving them out is better in my opinion. If that is the case, then the head weakens when its natural connection is disrupted, as we have seen with other body parts.
Especially when the patient's head is naturally weak, the first type of cauterization is safer and better in my opinion. Use it, and you will be safe if God wills.
The second chapter.
فيكيء الرأس أيضًا.
إذا حدث في جمجمة الرأس وجع مزمن وطال ذلك بالعليل واستعمل الإيارجات والقوقايات والسعوطات والأدهان والضمادات، ولا سيما إن كان قد كوى الكيّة الواحدة التي وصفنا فلم ينفعه شيء من ذلك فانظر. فإن كان رأس العليل قوي البنية بالطبع ولم يكن ضعيفا وكان يجد بردًا شديدًا فاكوه كيّة أخرى فوق تلك قليلا. ثم اكوه على كل قرن من رأسه كيّة حتى يذهب ثخن الجلد وينكشف من العظم القطر الذي وصفنا. واكوه كيّة في مؤخر رأسه في الموضع الذي يعرف بالفأس وخفف يدك في هذه ولا تكشف العظم فإن العليل يجد لها ألما شديدا خلاف ألم سائر كيّات الرأس كلها وسأذكر هذه الكيّة في موضعها.
ويجب أن تكون المكواة التي يكوى بها قرني الرأس ومؤخرته ألطف من المكواة التي يكوى بها وسط الرأس وهذه صورتها.
ال第三节章节。
For the acute migraine.
If pain and headache occur in the head split and the pain extends to the eye, induce vomiting with purgative medicines for the head and use all the treatments mentioned in the classifications of diseases. If this does not succeed, cauterization should be performed on it in two ways. Either cauterization with a sharp burning agent or with iron.
Cauterization with a burning agent is done by taking one clove of garlic, peeling it, and cutting its ends from both sides. Then, cut an incision in the location of the pain on the cheekbone using a broad scalpel until it reaches beneath the skin where the garlic can fit.
Insert it under the skin until it disappears, then wrap it securely with a bandage tightly. Leave it for fifteen hours, then remove the bandage and take out the garlic. Leave the wound for two or three days, then dress it.
Apply a cotton pad soaked in fat to the area until it becomes pus-filled, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If you prefer, you can do this with some burning medicines that I mentioned in Article Eighteen on burning medicines.
As for cauterization with iron, it is done in this manner: Heat the cautery tool which has this shape:.
It is called the screw-shaped cautery because its head resembles a nail, with some indentations and a small protrusion in the center.
Then place it on the site of the pain and hold your hand while you rotate the iron slightly, and the amount that you burn from the thickness of the skin should be like half of its thickness. Then raise your hand so that you do not burn the artery below, which would cause bleeding. Then soak a piece of cotton in salt water and place it on the site and leave it for three days. Then soak the cotton in oil, then treat it with ointment until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, cauterize this abscess with the heated blade of the cautery, and be careful not to cut the artery in this non-chronic abscess especially.
Chapter Four.
Treating Chronic Abscesses.
If you treat the abscess with the methods mentioned previously and what was discussed in the sections on diseases, and the treatment is ineffective, and you see that the condition requires something beyond what was mentioned of cauterization with medication or cauterization with fire. You should heat the cautery blade until it turns white. Then, mark along the site of the pain with a line about half a finger's width or so. Place your hand once and pull tight enough to cut the artery but not too deep to reach the bone.
However, you should be cautious not to touch the moving jaw during chewing, as burning the muscle or nerve that controls it can cause convulsions.
Be cautious and vigilant about the bleeding from the artery that you have cut, for there is danger in cutting it. Especially for one who is ignorant of what to do and has no tested experience; it is better to refrain from acting.
A discussion on how to manage bleeding from an artery will come in its proper place later in the book, if God wills. If you encounter a condition that cannot be addressed by this method, note it.
If you see that the patient's body can withstand it, apply a cautery in the middle of the head as described, and treat the wound until it heals, if God wills.
If you wish, use the cautery mentioned in the section on treating an artery with a double-bladed cautery, for it is a better and more effective method.
Chapter Five.
On the cautery for earaches.
If pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with laxatives and other treatments mentioned in the classification, but the pain does not subside, then heat the cautery called "al-nidhru," which has this shape.
Then, after heating it, apply it in dots around the entire ear as it circles, or around both ears if the pain is in both. Then, after applying the cauterization slightly away from the base of the ear, mark the spots with a coolant, and the cautery should consist of about ten dots in each ear or thereabouts. Then treat the spots until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Six.
فيك القوة.
The strength that is treated with cauterization is of the type that arises from phlegm, as I mentioned in the classifications of diseases.
Cauterization should be avoided for the type that arises from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you have treated this type of strength with iatrological methods, spongings, and gargles, and your treatment has not been effective, it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations. One at the base of the ear, the second a little below his temple, and the third where the lips meet.
Make the cauterization from the opposite side of the affected area because relaxation occurs on the seemingly healthy side.
The image of the cauterization is that you should cauterize once opposite the upper part of the ear, below the horn of the head a little, and another at the temple, and its length should be as long as the width of the thumb.
Lower your hand with the cautery until it burns to half the thickness of the skin. This is the image of the cautery, which is a type of knife-like instrument that was described earlier but is slightly finer as you can see. It should have a blade that is slightly thicker, then treat the area as previously described until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Seven.
About chronic paralysis.
If chronic paralysis persists despite the treatments mentioned and your treatment is ineffective, and there is no fever in the patient, apply four cauterizations. Apply one cauterization to each horn of the head, one cauterization in the middle of the head as mentioned, and one cauterization at the back of the head as previously described.
Apply the cauterizations as described. Additionally, cauterize one point at the mouth of the stomach, which will be more effective, then proceed with the treatments as previously described.
Chapter Eight.
About cauterization for forgetfulness.
Those who suffer from phlegm should be given large doses of ayargat (a type of medicine) and purifying pills for the brain initially.
Then, shave his entire head and apply a mustard plaster to the back of his head as described in the section on plasters. Do this multiple times, as it is equivalent to cauterization.
Follow the procedure exactly as mentioned there. If he recovers, that is sufficient; otherwise, cauterize him three times at the back of his head, arranged from the top of the head to the base of the neck.
Leave a space of one finger's width between each cauterization, then treat the cauterizations as previously described. If you wish to increase the treatment and the patient can tolerate it, perform an additional cauterization in the middle.
If you wish to increase it, remove it from the horns and then treat it until it heals, and the iron should be olive-colored as in the previous description.
Chapter Nine.
For treating hemiplegia and general relaxation of the body.
It is necessary to begin with cleansing the head with iatrological treatments as mentioned, then shave the patient's head and cauterize it with one cautery in the center of the head, one on each horn of the head, and one at the back.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck. If the condition of general relaxation of the body requires more than this, and if the patient can tolerate it and the disease is strong and persistent, cauterize him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of his back. Burn extensively until most of the skin is burned, then lift your hand and treat him as previously described until he heals, if God wills, and the cautery should be olive-colored.
Chapter Ten.
For treating epilepsy with cauterization.
A person with epilepsy caused by phlegm should be cauterized, and initially, his brain should be cleansed with major iatrological treatments and all other treatments mentioned in the classification if the patient is an adult and can tolerate taking medicines.
If the patient is a child who cannot tolerate medicines, then use gargles and purgatives that cleanse the brain several days before, along with improving their diet.
Then he shaves his head, then applies one cautery in the middle of the head as described in the description, and another cautery at the back of his head. And on each horn of his head, a cautery. If the patient is strong and can tolerate it, apply the cauterizations mentioned for one suffering from paralysis and relaxation of the body along the vertebrae of the neck and back; the cautery should be olive-colored as described previously.
If the patient is a child, then make the cautery gentle as described in this illustration.
Chapter Eleven.
On Cauterizing Mania.
If the cause of mania is putrid humidity and thick phlegm, apply the cauterizations mentioned for one suffering from paralysis.
If the cause of mania is excess that tends towards black bile and the patient's body is humidified, give him what purifies his brain as described in the division.
Then shave the patient's head, then make a tight pad of linen in the shape of a circle, and place it in the middle of his head while the patient is seated with his legs folded and holding onto something from all sides. Then take one pound of old lamb fat.
Then heat it over the fire to a moderate warmth, such that a finger can withstand it when inserted. Then pour it into the middle of his head in the circle and leave it until it cools. Do this for the patient once every week along with other proper treatment until he recovers, if God wills.
And if you wish, cauterize it with many small dots without holding the cautery in your hand, but rather let it be a light touch, for this kind of cauterization moistens the brain moderately.
Then apply cotton soaked in fat or chicken fat to it.
Chapter Twelve.
On cauterizing the watery discharge in the eye.
When you have identified the beginning of the watery discharge in the eye by the signs mentioned in the classification, then promptly treat the patient to cleanse his head and protect it from all moisture. Sweat him in the bath on an empty stomach for several days.
Then have him shave his head and cauterize it in the middle of the head, then cauterize two spots on the cheeks if the discharge starts from both eyes or one spot if it is from one eye.
Then cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries under the skin, and let the cauterizations be as long as the width of the cheeks, and be careful not to cause bleeding.
If you see any of it, cut it as needed by whatever treatment is possible. We will come to the wisdom in removing and cutting the arteries while being careful not to cause bleeding.
He may be cauterized at the back of the head under the two bones with two strong cauterizations.
Chapter Thirteen.
On cauterizing chronic tears.
If the tears of the eye are chronic and constant, and they come from the veins and arteries on the surface of the head outside the skull, and you are sure that this is due to excess cold phlegm, then use the cautery as I have described at the beginning of the flow of blood. Cauterize in the middle of the head and two places on each cheekbone, and two places at the back of the head under the two bones. If more is needed, cauterize one place on each side near the end of the eye at the edge of the eyebrow with a small cautery iron.
Chapter Fourteen.
On Cauterizing a Putrid Nose.
If the treatment mentioned in the division does not succeed, then immediately treat the patient with Cochlearia officinalis for three nights, then shave his head and cauterize the middle part with an olive oil cautery iron. Then cauterize with a screw-shaped cautery iron two places above the eyebrows under the hair slightly, and be careful not to cut the artery. This is an image of the screw-shaped cautery iron.
Chapter Fifteen.
On Cauterizing the Drooping Eyelid.
If the eyelid droops due to illness or moisture, cauterize the eyelid once with this crescent-shaped cautery iron.
If you wish, cauterize two places slightly above the eyebrows on each side, and keep a distance from the cheekbones. The length of each cautery mark should be as long as the eyebrow.
Do not overdo it with the cauterization; rather, do it to the extent that one-third of the skin burns. The shape of the cautery iron should be as follows.
Chapter Sixteen.
On Cauterizing the Eyelid.
If her eyelids turn inward, open the eye and cauterize it in two types. Cauterization can be done either with fire or with a burning medication. As for cauterizing with fire, instruct the patient to stop plucking their eyelashes if they do so, until they grow long and even.
If it turns inward at its base, bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they grow. When they have grown and are even, place the patient's head in your lap and mark the eyelid with ink in the shape of an oak leaf.
The marking should start near the eyelashes. Then place a cotton pad soaked in egg white or sparrow saliva under the eyelid, and heat the cautery iron whose shape is as described.
Then cauterize along the marked shape little by little in many sessions until the surface of the skin, which is in the shape of an oak leaf, is fully burned. The sign of a successful procedure is that the eyelid will retract and the hair will lift away from the eye socket.
At that point, lift your hand and leave it for three days. Then apply a cotton pad with grease to help the scab fall off, and treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If some hair regrows after some time and the eyelid relaxes again.
Repeat the cautery on that place as you did initially. If the hair is in the lower eyelid, pluck it until it returns to its natural position without piercing the eye. As for cauterization with a burning drug, order the patient to leave the eyelashes so they grow long and straight.
Then make a paper figure of an oak leaf. Take one drachma or so each of the usual soap and unslaked lime, and grind them together finely. Do this in a mortar so that they do not dry out. Then apply it to the paper you made in the shape of an oak leaf and place it on one or both eyelids. Place a piece of cotton soaked in egg white under the eye, and have the patient's head in your lap.
Place your index finger above the medicine and press it lightly while moving it whenever the patient feels a tingling from the medicine, as he will feel a burning sensation like fire. As long as the patient feels this tingling, leave the medicine in place and move it with your finger. When the tingling subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
Observe, and if you see the eyelid raised as it would be when cauterized with fire or cut, then do nothing further. If not, repeat applying the medicine to the area that was unaffected by the medicine and did not darken until you complete your work and cauterize the eye. Then place cotton soaked in fat on it until the burning irritation subsides.
Then treat it with a cream such as the palm-based one or another until it heals. When working, be extremely careful that no part of the medicine falls into the eye. If the eyelid relaxes after days and you suspect any hair in the eye.
Prepare the medicine on that part of the eyelid that has relaxed as you did initially, then treat it until it heals. This is a picture of an oak leaf.
Know that people's eyes differ in size, so adjust accordingly. The way of correctness is not hidden from those who have experience in this craft.
Chapter Seventeen.
On cauterizing the nasal abscess that occurs in the duct of the eye.
If you treat the abscess as mentioned in the sections on diseases and your treatment is not effective, it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and have a servant hold the patient's head still so that it does not move or shake.
Then place a cotton pad moistened in the white of an egg or in the saliva of a weasel on his eyes, then heat the cautery, which is depicted here.
Make the cautery hollow, like the shape of a eagle feather from one end where the cauterization will occur. If you prefer, it can be perforated at the other end, or solid like a rod; however, this hollow type is better for your work, if God wills.
Then squeeze the abscess if it is open and remove the pus, then dry it. If it is not open, cut it open and remove its pus. Then place the hot cautery on it immediately; hold it with your hand until it reaches the bone.
Move your hand a little away from the eye towards the nose when cauterizing so that you do not miss or disturb the patient causing the cautery iron to fall into the eyelid and damage it. If you reach the bone at the beginning of the cautery, otherwise repeat the cautery once if necessary.
Leave it for three days, then apply a bandage with grease and treat it with the dried ointment until it heals. If after forty days it has not healed, then apply a sharp medicinal treatment until the bone is exposed, and proceed as will be mentioned in its chapter, God willing.
Another approach to cauterizing a fistula, mentioned by some early practitioners, is to deliberately cut open the area of the fistula and then place a thin tube in the same incision; this is its illustration.
Pour in an amount equal to the weight of one dirham of melted lead and hold the tube firmly with a tight grip, and the patient must not move at all so that the melted lead does not flow into his eye. It is advisable to place a cotton pad soaked in egg white or water on the patient's eye.
For the lead will burn the area of the fistula and heal it miraculously. If the fistula heals as mentioned using cauterization and treatment, otherwise it is necessary to use nasal puncture and redirect the fistula into the nasal passage as will be described in its specific section.
Chapter Eighteen.
On Cauterizing a Cleft Lip.
Often, a cleft occurs in the lip called al-sihat, especially in the lips of children. It often happens that when you treat this cleft as mentioned in the division [of the text], if the treatment does not succeed, heat a small knife-like iron smoothing tool in this manner.
Make the inside as thin as the blade of a knife, then place it while hot into the same cleft until the cauterization reaches the depth of the cleft, then treat it with the quilator until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Nineteen.
On cauterizing fresh fistulas in the mouth.
If a swelling occurs at the base of the gum or on the palate or at the roots of the teeth, and it becomes abscessed and bursts, resulting in a fistula from the pus flow, then if you treat it and the treatment is not successful, you should heat an iron cautery to fit the size of the fistula.
Then insert it hot into the fistula hole and hold it until the heated iron reaches its depth and end. Do this once or twice, then treat it afterward with the treatments mentioned until it heals, if God wills.
If the substance is interrupted and it heals, otherwise, it is necessary to examine the place and remove the diseased bone as will be mentioned in its chapter, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty.
On cauterizing loose teeth and gums.
If the gums have loosened due to moisture and the teeth have become loose, and you have treated them with medicines but they were ineffective, then place the patient's head in your lap, then heat the cautery that its image will come after this, after placing the tube on the tooth.
Insert the hot cautery into it quickly, and hold your hand for a little while until the patient feels that the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth. Then lift your hand and insert the cautery again as many times as you wish. Then have the patient rinse his mouth with salt water.
Hold it for an hour and then spit it out. The loose tooth will become stable, the relaxed gum will tighten, and the harmful moisture will dry up.
Chapter Twenty-One.
On Treating Toothache.
If the toothache is due to cold or there are worms in the tooth and medication has not been effective, then cauterization is done in two ways: either by using fat or by using fire.
Cauterization with fat is done by taking beef tallow and boiling it in an iron ladle or a shell. Then take a piece of cotton, wrap it on the end of a probe, dip it into the boiled fat, and quickly place it on the painful tooth, holding it until it cools.
Then repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. If you prefer, you can dip a piece of wool or cotton in cold fat and place it on the painful tooth, then put a heated iron over it until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
And as for cauterization with fire, it is that you take a copper or iron tube, and it should have some thickness so that the heat of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth. Then heat the cautery, which will be depicted in its form, and place it on the tooth itself; hold your hand until the cautery cools down, and do this repeatedly.
And the pain will go either that very day or the next. After this cauterization, the patient should fill his mouth with good fat and hold it for an hour before spitting it out. This is the image of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish, as much as possible. This is the image of the tube.
Chapter Twenty-Two.
On Cauterizing Pigs.
If the pigs are affected by phlegm and cold moisture and do not respond to maturity through medications, and you wish for rapid maturation, then heat the hollow cautery, whose image is shown here, with both ends perforated.
To allow smoke to exit from the other end during cauterization, place it protectively on the same tumor once or twice if necessary until it reaches the depth of the tumor. If the tumor is small, make the cautery proportionate to the size of the tumor.
Then leave it for three days and apply a cotton pad soaked in fat until what was burned by the fire is healed, then treat it with ointment and bandages until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Twenty-Three.
في كيّ البحة وضيق النفس.
إذا غلبت الرطوبات على قصبة الرئة ولا سيما إذا كان ذلك مع برودة المزاج، فينبغي أن يستفرغ العليل أولًا بالأدوية المسهلة، ثم تكويه كيّة في نقرة النحر عند أصل الحلقوم في الموضع المنخفض.
فاحذر أن تصل بالكي إلى الحلقوم ولا تحرق من الجلد إلا نصفة، ثم اكوه كيّة أخرى عند مفصل العنق في آخر خرزة منه بليغة وتكون المكواة مسمارية على الصفة التي تقدمت.
ثم عالجه بما تقدم ذكره حتى يبرأ إن شاء الله.
Chapter Twenty-Four.
في كيّ مرض الرئة والسعال.
إذا كان السعال ومرض الرئة عن رطوبات باردة ولم يكن بالعليل حمى ولا سل وكان المرض مزمنا فاكوه كيّتين فوق الترقوتين في المواضع المنخفضة اللينة الفارغة وكيّة أخرى في وسط الصدر بين الثديين.
وتكون المكواة مسمارية على الصورة التي تقدمت، وإن شئت فليكثف كيّه بالنقاط بالمكواة التي تسمى النقطة وقد تقدّمت صورتها في تنقيط وجع الأذنين وتكون النقط من ثلاثين نقطة إلى نحوها.
Then treat it as previously described until it heals. You can also make a tongued cautery with three prongs as shown in this figure, and use it quickly because you can cauterize three areas at once with it, and here is the figure of the cautery.
Chapter Twenty-Five.
On Cauterizing the Armpit.
If the head of the humerus dislocates due to slippery rheumatics or does not stabilize when it is reduced, so that it becomes habitual for it to dislocate with even slight movement as we have observed, then the shoulder should be reduced first. Then the patient should lie on his back or on the affected side. Then raise the skin inside the armpit upwards with your left fingers if the joint has dislocated inwardly.
Then heat the double-bladed cautery whose figure is shown here.
Then cauterize the skin with it until it penetrates to the other side, forming four cautery marks. It can also be cauterized with a three-pronged cautery, in which case six cautery marks will form, and the prongs should be placed on the thin part of the skin.
And this is the figure of the three-pronged cautery.
It can also include one more, making the cautery marks eight. Then apply cauterized seeds ground with salt to the area, and the patient should remain immobile for a period of time until it strengthens. If the dislocation is upward, which is rare.
A single good nail-shaped cautery above the shoulder or many dotted cauteries, for the joint will strengthen, moisture will disappear, and the patient will be cured.
Chapter Twenty-Six.
On Cauterizing the Stomach.
If cold and excessive moisture occur in the stomach, causing it to deviate from its normal condition and leading to frequent downward discharges, and if various treatments have been ineffective, the patient should lie on his back with arms and legs extended, and then three cauterizations should be applied. A nail-shaped cautery should be applied under the chest spoon by the width of a finger, and two cauterizations below each side of the single cautery until their shape forms a triangle, with sufficient distance between them to prevent them from meeting if they become pus-filled. The depth of the cautery should be one-third the thickness of the skin, and this is the shape of the cauterizations.
In this manner and to this extent, without addition.
If you prefer, apply one large cautery in the center of the stomach in this manner.
The cautery instrument used for this single cautery should be in the shape of a circle as shown.
The stomach may also be cauterized with dotted cauteries for those who are anxious about the large cautery. This involves marking dots on the stomach in the desired quantity with a solution, then applying a dotted-shaped cautery, followed by treatment as previously described until recovery occurs.
Chapter Twenty-Seven.
Regarding the cold biliary temperament.
If pain occurs in the liver due to cold and moisture, or due to a noxious vapor such that it deviates from its natural temperament excessively, and the patient is treated with what was mentioned in the classification but to no avail. The patient should lie on his stomach, and three cauteries should be applied with a cautery fluid in this shape and exactly this size on the liver, below the armpits where a person's forearm ends.
Each cauterization should be about the thickness of a finger apart from the previous one. The cauterization should be straight along the length of the body. Do not hold the cautery tool too tightly, but rather loosely.
The amount of the skin thickness that should be burned is half its thickness, no more. The patient should stand on both feet; if he cannot stand, he should lie down with his legs extended and arms raised. This is a picture of the cautery tool.
You may apply these cauterizations with a knife cautery if you are skilled and careful in the practice to avoid excessive burning, which could burn through the skin entirely and reach the intestines, as the skin there is thin. Be aware of this.
Chapter Twenty-Eight.
Regarding the cauterization of swelling in the liver.
If an abscess appears in the liver and you want to determine whether the swelling is in the liver tissue or in its membrane, if it is in the liver tissue, then the patient will feel heavy pain without sharpness.
And if it is in the region of the liver, there is a very sharp pain, and I have seen that its treatment has exhausted the skills of physicians. It is necessary for the patient to lie on his back, then apply hot compresses to the affected area.
Then heat the iron in the fire; this is the iron that resembles a mel (a tool similar to a knife or curved blade), and here is its image. Burn it with one cautery until the skin is completely burned, and continue the cauterization until you reach the peritoneum so that all of it comes out, then treat it as you would treat an abscess until he recovers.
This type of cauterization should not be used except by those who have long experience in the practice of medicine and have repeatedly encountered these diseases through experience. At that point, they may proceed with such a procedure, though I prefer to avoid it.
Chapter Twenty-Nine.
On Cauterizing Appendicitis.
I have described earlier the cauterization for cold appendicitis using the root of the zarawnad in this manner: take one root of the dry and long zarawnad, as thick as a finger, and make it as long as possible. Then dip it in oil and light it in the fire. Then burn it with one cautery between the connection of the clavicle and the neck, and two small cauterizations slightly below the jugular veins on the side under the chin, and two large cauterizations above the breasts between the third and fourth ribs.
And cauterizations also between the fifth and sixth ribs slightly inclined backward, another in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach, and three cauterizations from behind one between the shoulders and two at the sides of the spine below the cautery which is between the shoulders.
You should not penetrate deeply with the cautery but rather keep it on the surface of the skin for a smearing effect. Some early authors mentioned that there were people who used an iron cautery shaped like a needle, heating it and inserting it between the ribs until it reached the tumor itself.
And the duration is as mentioned for a liver tumor. Cauterizing this area carries great risks; either the patient may die immediately, or an incurable fistula may develop in the affected area.
Chapter Thirty.
On Cauterizing the Spleen.
If you treat a spleen disease with the methods mentioned in the division and your treatment is not effective, then cauterize it in three ways, all of which are correct. One way is to cauterize it with three or four cauteries arranged along the length of the spleen.
Arrange them like the cauteries of the liver, whose form has been described previously. The distance between each cauterization should be the thickness of a finger or slightly more. The shape of the cautery should be as mentioned for cauterizing the liver. Do not penetrate deeply with the cautery, and the patient should lie on his back.
Another approach is at the left armpit. Raise the skin opposite the spleen where the patient's left arm ends, and raise the skin across the width of the body so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert the cauteries very carefully until they penetrate the skin from the other side, then remove the cautery; there will be four cauterizations. If you wish, use the other cautery with three cauteries.
Then treat the cauterized area after leaving it to suppurate for many days, as this is more effective than other previously mentioned treatments.
Chapter Thirty-One.
On Cauterizing Ascites.
Cauterization is beneficial specifically for dropsical ascites. If you treat the patient with various treatments we have mentioned in the classification and they are ineffective, then you should cauterize four cauteries around the navel and one on the abdomen.
Another cautery on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind his back between the shoulder blades, one opposite his chest and another opposite his abdomen. The depth of the cauterization should be close to the thickness of the skin, then leave the wound open to suppurate for a long time.
Do not neglect treatment for the patient after cauterization with what is necessary to achieve both purposes and thus hasten recovery. The shape of the cautery used on the back should be screw-shaped as previously described, and the one used on the abdomen should be olive-shaped.
Chapter Thirty-Two.
On Cauterizing the Feet and Legs.
If they become swollen in the edematous area and are filled with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot at the indentation between the little toe and the ring toe.
Keep your hand steady with the cautery and do not tilt it, then raise your hand without returning it at all, for the yellow water will drain. The cautery should be in this form.
Then cauterize on each leg with two cauteries; the cautery should be done using the sharp end of the cautery and should be applied along the length of the leg, one above the knee and another below it towards the middle of the thigh. On each thigh, apply two cauteries.
Leave the cauterization open without treatment for a long time, during which water will drain from it, then treat it with all that has been mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
On Cauterizing Diarrhea.
If diarrhea is caused by cold and moisture, which weaken the forces of retention and digestion in the stomach and intestines, and if it has been treated with various methods without recovery, and you see that the patient can withstand cauterization and has abundant strength, cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach. As mentioned earlier for cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery and four gentle cauterizations around the navel using a fine spiral cautery, apply one large or two cauterizations on the cotton above the buttocks.
If you see that the moisture is abundant and the patient can withstand it, cauterize him with one cautery on each thigh fold, one on each flank, and perhaps add two small cauterizations near the large one on the stomach. This treatment is effective and its benefit should not be missed, if God wills.
Chapter Thirty-Four.
Regarding hemorrhoids of the rectum.
If there are chronic hemorrhoids in the rectum, whether numerous or singular, and they are of thick, cold mixtures or corrupt humors, and if treatment according to what was mentioned in the classification has been ineffective, then apply three cauterizations on the lower part of the spinal cord, slightly below the table (a reference to a specific anatomical landmark), in a triangular pattern.
Apply a cauterization two fingerbreadths below the navel. If you determine that his stomach has become cold and that his food is not digesting, and if you observe his face as swollen, then apply a large cauterization on the stomach as previously described, and also apply a cauterization on his liver. Apply another cauterization on his spleen using a spiral cautery. Leave the cauterization open for some time, then treat him until he is cured, if God wills.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
Regarding cauterization of warts.
After cutting it, if the wart has been cut, heat the cautery that resembles a needle and insert it while hot into the same cut wart. Proceed carefully until the cautery reaches the opening of the sweat gland from which blood flows. Do this once or twice.
If the warts are numerous, apply one cauterization to each as described, then treat them with appropriate ointments until they heal. If you cauterize it larger on a piece of cotton, it will be more effective.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
关于发生在臀部及其周围的瘘管的情况。
如果病人对所描述的切开和治疗过程感到害怕而拒绝执行，或许可以通过烧烙疗法使其康复。当一个人患有瘘管并且脓液和其他腐败液体从中流出时，首先你应该用一根细探针来测量它。
然后，用探针了解瘘管的深度，接着加热一个类似铲形的烙铁，将其插入瘘管中，插入的深度应与探针测量的一致，并沿着瘘管的深度进行烧烙，直到所有腐败物质都被烧尽，根据需要可能需要重复一到三次。
要注意不要烧伤神经，如果有神经存在的话，也不要烧伤大的腺体。如果瘘管通向膀胱或肠道的器官也要小心。
要小心所有这些部位，如果瘘管位于肉厚且你觉得不易穿透的地方，则应进行治疗直到伤口愈合。如果伤口封闭并且没有分泌物排出，并保持这种状态一段时间，那么你可以知道它已经完全康复。
如果没有停止分泌物，那么你可以知道它仍然穿透或者其深处有腐败的骨头或其他类似的情况，在相关内容的位置会有进一步说明。
Chapter Thirty-Seven.
关于烧烙肾脏的方法。
如果肾脏因为寒冷或强烈的风而疼痛，并且导致病人的整体状况下降，那么应该在背部对受影响的肾脏进行烧烙治疗。使用之前提到的类似螺丝刀形状的烙铁，在每侧肾脏各烧烙一次，有时甚至在同一张桌子上进行第三次烧烙，这样总共三次烧烙会排列在一起，效果更佳。
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
On the Treatment of Bladder Stones.
If the bladder becomes weak and relaxed due to cold and humidity, such that the patient cannot retain urine, cauterize it with cautery at the lower part of the navel near the bladder, where pubic hair begins. Cauterize also on the right side of the navel and on the left side.
After the cauterization from each side, it should be done to the extent of the width of a thumb joint. Cauterize once at the lower back or twice if necessary. The cautery tool should be needle-like as previously described.
Chapter Thirty-Nine.
On the Cauterization of the Uterus.
If cold and humidity cause a substance in the uterus that prevents conception, corrupts the fetus, or causes pain during its emergence, it is necessary to cauterize with three cauteries around the navel as described for the cauterization of the bladder. Cauterize once at the base of the spine on the cotton or twice if necessary, and the cautery tool should be needle-like.
Chapter Forty.
On the Cauterization for Dislocated Hip.
Humid phlegm can lead to a dislocation of the hip joint, causing one leg to become longer than the other when compared. If you find an empty space indicating the dislocation, it is necessary to cauterize the affected area around the hip itself with a semi-circular cautery.
After learning with ink around the truth as it rotates so that the same truth falls in the center of the circle, then if this iron is not available to you, cauterize three times with a large olive-shaped cautery.
Make the cauterization depth according to the thickness of the entire skin, then treat it until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Forty-One.
On Cauterizing for Sciatica.
If pain occurs in the hip joint and its cause is cold and humidity, and treating the patient with what was mentioned in the classification of treatments does not improve the condition and persists, it is necessary to facilitate for the patient by using foul-smelling herbs or prickly lettuce and similar substances.
Then cauterize him, and the cauterization should be in two ways: either by using caustic drugs or by fire. Cauterization with fire can be done in many ways; one of them is to cauterize on the hip joint itself three triangular cauteries as shown in this illustration.
Make the depth suitable for them, and the distance between each cauterization should be equal to the thickness of a finger. The cautery should be olive-shaped. You may also cauterize one cauterization in the center on top of the hip joint itself, making four cauteries in total. If you wish, you can use the circular method mentioned earlier for dislocated hips and perform one cauterization.
The circle should encompass the entire hip and burn through the entire thickness of the skin. This is the method of cauterization for sciatica if the pain is fixed to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh or leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, burn two cauteries on the thigh at the place where the patient points out as painful; one cauterization above the heelbone by four fingers towards the lateral side slightly. The cautery should be knife-shaped, and the depth of the cauterization should be only as thick as the skin.
If he points out that the pain extends towards his toes, burn three or four or more dots where he indicates with a cautery. If he points to the pain below the knee towards the leg, burn one knife-shaped cauterization there.
Be careful in all cauterizations that the cautery does not reach a nerve or large artery, as this could cause a serious harm or long-term illness to the patient.
I have seen one and two cases where cauterization was performed above the heelbone and overcautery led to severe swelling in the leg, extending down to the foot, perforating it entirely, and ruining the entire limb. Diarrhea and death followed thereafter. If the pain is on both sides, I would cauterize them in this exact manner.
Some scholars among the philosophers mentioned that for cauterizing the hip, a cautery of this description should be made: fashion something like a cup from iron, with its diameter being half a palm width, and at its mouth it should be as thick as a date pit or slightly less. Inside that cup there is another cup, and a third one inside that.
The space between each cup should be the width of a thumb joint, and the cups should be open on both sides. Their height should be about one or two joints. A handle made of iron should be firmly attached to the cups, and this is its shape.
Then it is heated in the fire until it becomes red and sparks fly, then it is placed on the right hip and the patient lies on their healthy side. It should be cauterized with three circular burns at once, then leave it for three days and dress it with grease, leaving the wound open for several days.
It is rarely used because of its ugliness and the horror of its appearance, and because few are found who can endure it; however, it is one of the excellent types of cauterization for those who can endure it and whose condition warrants it.
As for cauterization with burning drugs, it is done by making two cups resembling the sockets into which door hinges fit, made of copper or iron.
There should be a height of about two fingers or so around each one, and the distance between them should be the width of a finger. They should be open at the bottom and open at the top, and they should be held together in this manner.
Then place them on the right hip with the patient lying on their healthy side. Keep your hand well wrapped, then pour a little hot water that has been heated in the fire between the two circles. Hold it for about one hour as measured by an hourglass. The patient must endure its stinging and burning, for they will feel a sting like fire.
Until the stinging subsides, then lift your hand from the tool and wipe all the affected area with fresh water. Then leave it for three days and apply grease to it until the blackness of the burn fades away. Leave it for several days so that pus can drain out; this is more effective in healing.
Then treat it with ointments until he recovers. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a splint for him as you did for the hip, similarly keeping water out. This is the description of the sharp water and I have established it in the article on preparing medicines.
Take one part each of frying salt and unslaked lime, crush them, and place them in a new pot which you have pierced with a single small hole at the bottom, according to the size of the amount that can enter through it. Place another glazed pot under the bottom of the pot.
Pour fresh water over the salt and lime to cover them by one finger, after kneading them well with your hand. Leave the pot until the sharp water drips into the glazed pot below. Then collect all this water and pour it over another portion of lime and salt that have been renewed as well.
It will then be very sharp and effective for many medical tasks and for cauterizing other parts, as it acts like fire itself. There are also medicines used for cauterizing the hip, such as thapsia, bladder syrup, and lime with soap, which are boiled together.
Galen tells a story about an ancient man who had a remedy for hip pain and sciatica, and he highly praised it, claiming that no other treatment is needed and that it cures in one application.
Indeed, it is said that a person might enter the bathhouse carried and leave cured. This remedy involves taking green silphium; if not available, dry recent silphium can be used. Crush it finely with some fat and apply it to the hip where the pain is, or on the leg or thigh.
And it should be tightened and left for three hours or as long as the patient feels that the burning has stopped, then take him to the bathhouse. When his body is drenched with sweat, put him in the pool; the pain will disappear and he will be healed by God's permission. If he does not heal, redo the dressing on him after ten days once again.
He will be healed, if God wills. And know that one should not use cauterization with these medicines until the body has been purged. Dioscorides mentioned that the sweat of a goat, when used for cauterization on sciatica, is beneficial.
Cauterization should be performed in this manner: Take wool, soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep spot between the thumb and the joint of the hand, closer to the joint. Then take dry sweat from a goat.
Set it alight with fire until it becomes an ember, then place it on the wool and leave it until it extinguishes. Then take another one; continue doing this until the sensation reaches halfway between the shoulder and the hip. The pain will be relieved by God's permission. This type of cauterization is called caprine cauterization.
Chapter Forty-Two.
On Cauterizing Back Pain.
Pain in the back may occur due to many reasons, such as a fall or a blow or excessive purging and similar causes. It is caused by the accumulation of cold and moist substances, and cauterization is applied specifically to this type.
Whoever suffers from the effusion of cold matter should, after inducing vomiting with rotten fruit and similar substances, cauterize his back at the site of pain in three rows as wide as a table, applying five or more cauteries in each row according to what the patient can tolerate and his strength.
The cauterization should be done with a puncture iron. If you prefer, you can perform it with three or four cauteries using a medium-sized nail iron in this manner.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
On Cauterizing the Initial Stage of a Hunchback.
This condition often occurs in young children, and its initial sign is that the child experiences shortness of breath when standing or moving. You will find a protruding vertebra at the end of the spine that stands out compared to the other vertebrae.
If you observe this and wish to prevent its progression, cauterize it with an iron in the shape of a circle as shown in this illustration. Cauterize the vertebra evenly on all sides. If you prefer, you can perform it around the vertebra using a puncture iron in two or three rows, with the punctures close to each other. Then treat the area until it heals as mentioned.
Be cautious not to use cauterization in a hunchback caused by nerve spasms.
Chapter Forty-Four.
On Cauterizing Gout and Joint Pains.
If the pains in the joints are due to cold humidities that settle in any part of the body, and if these pains occur in the legs, it is the custom of physicians to call this gout.
If the cold gout is treated with various treatments that we have mentioned in the classification and the pains do not subside, then cauterization will remove them. This involves cauterizing around the knee joints after vomiting, using many cauteries. The cautery should be olive-shaped and medium-sized, as shown in this illustration.
If it is necessary to puncture the face of the foot, do so with a puncturing cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, which often happens, cauterize each knee with three or four cauteries from each side using this olive-shaped cautery.
If more cauterization is needed, proceed with it, but do not go deep with the cautery; it should only be as thick as the skin. If the pains ascend to the hips or back, use the cauterization methods mentioned in that section.
If the pains are in the hands only, puncture around the wrists in two rows. If the pains remain in the fingers, puncture each joint with a point and on the heel of the hand. If the pains ascend to the elbows or shoulders after days, proceed accordingly.
Cauterize them from each side, and do not neglect proper care and taking medicine. If the patient improves their diet and expels phlegm, they will recover with this cauterization, God willing.
Chapter Forty-five.
في خياطة الفتحات.
إذا ظهر فتق في الأربية وانحدرت بعض أجزاء المعاء والثرب إلى الخصية وكان الفتق مبتدئاً قريباً، فينبغي أن تأمر المريض بترك الأكل لمدة يوم وأن يستخدم من الملينات ما يساعد على إخراج البراز من جوفه.
ثم يضطجع بين يديك على ظهره وتأمره أن يمسك نفسه حتى يبرز الثرب أو المعاء، ثم تردده بأصبعك. ثم تعلم بالمداد تحت الفتق على عظم العانة علامة تشبه نصف الدائرة أطرافها إلى أعلى البدن.
ثم تحمى مكواة، وهذه صورتها.
حتى تCOME WHITE وتخلو من الشرر، ثم ترد المعاء أو الثرب إلى جوفه. ثم يضع خادم يده على الموضع لئلا يبرز المعاء، وقد فرجت بين ساقى المريض ووضعت تحته وسادة، وخادم آخر يربط ساقيه.
وثالث على صدره يمسك يديه، ثم تنزل المكواة على العلامة نفسها. وتضرب بالمكواة واقفة مستقيمة، وتمسكها حتى تبلغ بها العظم أو تعدها مرة أخرى إن لم تبلغ بالأولى إلى العظم.
وتحفظ جهدك من بروز المعاء في حين خياطتك لئلا تحرقه فيحدث بذلك للمريض إما الموت وإما بلية عظمى. واعلم أنك متى لم تبلغ بالخياطة العظم لم ينجح عملك، ويجب أن تكون مكواة الصبيان لطيفة على أقدارهم وللكبار على أقدارهم.
Then treat the cauterized area after three days with fat until the redness of the fire subsides, then treat it with other ointments until it heals. Let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is completely healed.
It is advisable to make his diet during the treatment such that it softens his stomach so that the intestines do not protrude when defecating. Then, if he wants to stand up after forty days, use a firm bandage and keep him bound for another forty days, and reduce his exertion and fullness from food and drink and loud shouting.
If this treatment is followed as described, he will be completely healed, God willing. I will mention the treatment of hernias by incision in its proper section, God willing. As for a hernia that occurs in other parts of the abdomen and is recent, if you wish it not to worsen, apply cautery in the form of a circle according to its size from the hernia. Burn a portion of the skin, about one-third, then treat it as mentioned. It will not worsen, God willing. Some early practitioners have suggested using a triangular cautery on the hernia in this manner.
After treating the hernia with collyrium, draw a line across at the top of the hernia and another line downwards. Place your hand in the middle and apply one cautery in the shape of a nail. The first method is easier and better, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Six.
On Cautering Hydrocele.
If there is pain in some organs due to a fall or a blow, and the pain persists for a long time without medicine being effective, it should be cauterized with a cautery point. The burning of each organ should be according to its size, whether large or small, and according to its weakness or strength.
If the pain persists despite the initial cauterization, repeat the cauterization because it is characteristic of such pains to move to adjacent organs. Therefore, follow them with cauterization until the patient recovers.
Chapter Forty-Seven.
On Cauterizing Leprosy.
Leprosy patients can greatly benefit from cauterization, especially those whose condition is due to the putrefaction of phlegm and black bile.
If you wish to cauterize a leprosy patient, examine them. If the leprosy is in its initial stage and has not improved with the treatments mentioned in the classification, and if there is fear that the disease might spread throughout their constitution, then cauterize the head with five applications. The first one in the middle of the head, the second below it near the forehead at the end of the hair, two on the temples, and one from behind on the nape of the neck. Cauterize deeply so that it slightly affects the bone.
Scabs will fall off, making it easier for thick vapors to escape. Cauterize him again in the same manner as described for the spleen. If leprosy persists and becomes clearly visible, cauterize the areas on the head as mentioned earlier. A cautery mark at the tip of the nose and two on each cheek, two on the cervical vertebrae, six on the thoracic and lumbar vertebrae, one large one at the coccyx at the base of the tailbone and another above it in the same region, and two on the hipbones, one on each side. Two on the knees, one on each knee, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the ribs of the chest, and a cautery mark on every joint of his fingers and toes, and one on the heel of each foot and one on each wrist.
Be cautious of the nerve at the back of the heels to avoid burning it. A cautery mark may be applied on the pubic bone, another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver. Know that the more you apply cauteries, the more effective they are.
Know that the sick person does not feel pain from cautery as a healthy person would, because his body is numb. The cauteries should be made with large or small instruments according to the organs and joints, as previously described for the characteristics of the tools.
Then treat the cautery with flour of barley mixed with honey and continue other treatments until he is healed, if God wills.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
On Cauterizing Numbness: If a part of the body becomes numb and is treated with medicines, ointments, and dressings but does not heal, then cauterize the numb part with cautery marks according to what the bone or joint deserves in size. Make your cautery deeper into the thickness of the skin slightly.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals, and for some numbness that occurs in the hand or foot near the vertebrae of the spine where the nerve that moves that limb exits, cauterization may be applied to alleviate the numbness.
And he should not proceed with that except for one who is well-versed in the anatomy of organs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
On Cauterizing Vitiligo.
If vitiligo persists and no medical remedy proves effective, cauterize it slightly to a depth equal to the thickness of the skin, so that the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with flour of lentils mixed with rose oil, rue leaves, the tongue of a pregnant hen, and the blood of a pigeon or sparrow, using one part of each. Mix all together and apply to a bandage which is then applied to the affected area until it heals.
Chapter Fifty.
On Cauterizing Cancer.
If the cancer is in its early stages and you wish to stop its progression, cauterize it with a circular iron around it as it rotates. Some wise men have mentioned that it should be cauterized deeply in the center, but I do not see this as advisable because I expect it to ulcerate, and I have witnessed this happen several times.
The proper method is to cauterize around it in a circle as we have said, or with many small cauterizations.
Chapter Fifty-One.
In Treating Hernias.
If a hernia occurs and it delays in maturing, either due to the active quality that causes it, or due to the age of the patient if he is an elderly person with little blood, or due to time, and you wish to hasten the maturation of the hernia, then apply numerous small cauterizations around it, dotting them.
Then leave it, for it will mature more quickly. If you wish to treat it with cauterization, heat the cautery, which has this shape.
Place it in the center of the hernia until it penetrates the skin. Let the cauterization be from below to facilitate the flow of pus, then treat it as necessary until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
In Cauterizing Ulcers.
An ulcer is a corruption that spreads within the organ, eating it as fire consumes dry wood. If you see an ulcer in a place where cauterization with fire is possible, heat many cautery irons of various sizes—small and large—as appropriate for the location of the ulcer.
Then cauterize it from all sides until all the corruption is completely removed and nothing remains. Then leave it for three days, and apply powdered sulfur mixed with oil to the cauterized areas until all the scabs and corruption fall off entirely.
Then treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth. If, after three days, you see that the flesh is growing properly without any corruption, proceed otherwise, repeat the cauterization on the remaining corrupt areas. The ulcer can also be treated with a potent medication.
For it takes the place of fire more quickly and effectively. I have mentioned its treatment with a sharp medicine in the classification, so take it from there when you need it.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
On Heating Reverse and Non-Reverse Nails.
This condition often occurs on the soles of the feet; it is rough and causes pain. Heating to treat it can be done in two ways: either by fire or by boiling water.
As for heating with fire, it involves heating a hollow iron tool resembling an eagle's feather, which is made to fit around the nail on all sides and has thin edges. Then place the heated tool onto the nail and rotate your hand around the nail with the tool until it reaches the depth of the nail.
Leave it for three days until pus forms, then dress it with crushed wild barley mixed with salt. Leave the dressing on overnight; the nail will come out from its root. Then treat the wound site with a healing ointment until it heals. If the nails are not reversed.
This often occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet. You should take a tube made of copper or iron or an eagle's feather and place it over the nail or growth, then pour some boiling water into the tube.
Hold the tube with your hand and rotate it while gently pressing to ensure the edge of the tube affects the root of the nail. The boiling water will find its way to reach the depth of the nail. The patient should忍耐一会儿沸水的刺痛。
Then leave it, for the nail will come off with its root. Do this one by one until you have dealt with all of them in the body, then treat their places after they are removed with ointments that promote flesh growth.
Chapter Forty-Four.
On Scorching the Sponge.
If one of the sponge carriers is affected by cold in the nerve or by a quarter fever or something else, it is necessary to scorch him four or five times on the acupuncture points on the back, with a scorching at each point, and also scorch once on his chest. And scorch his stomach with an olive oil heated iron, for the sponge carrier will be relieved and the cold illness will quickly mature.
Chapter Forty-Five.
On Scorching Boils That Occur in the Body.
Boils may appear in the body due to thick, corrupt cold substances. At their first appearance, it is necessary to scorch each boil gently with a burning end of an ash branch or with the root of a long rue stem or with a lentil-shaped iron on top of the boil.
Veins that become inflamed at their initial onset can also be scorcheded in this manner, so they do not increase and the causative factor causing them dissipates, leading to the patient's recovery. However, it should be done after letting blood from the patient.
Chapter Forty-Six.
On severe bleeding from cutting the artery.
Severe bleeding often occurs when an artery is cut during a wound that has been exposed from the outside, or when incising a tumor or organ and the like; it is difficult to control.
If such a situation occurs, quickly place your thumb on the mouth of the artery and press firmly so that the blood is confined under your finger and does not escape. Then heat olive oil cauterizing irons of various sizes in the fire until they become very hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large depending on the wound and the location where the artery has burst. Place the iron on the same vein immediately after removing your finger quickly, holding the iron until the bleeding stops.
If the bleeding continues when you remove your finger from the mouth of the artery and before using the iron, quickly take another iron from those in the prepared fire and continue doing so with one after another until the bleeding stops.
Be careful not to burn a nerve that may be nearby, as this would cause additional harm to the patient. Know that if blood flows from an artery, it cannot be cut except by one of four methods: cauterization as we have described, or amputation if it has not already been done. If it is amputated, the ends will contract and the bleeding will stop. Alternatively, it can be tightly ligatured with threads, or medications that cause hemostasis can be applied and firmly bandaged to stop the bleeding.
As for those who attempt to cut it with a ligature or by binding with cloth or applying burning substances and the like, it will not be severed by that at all except in rare cases. If any of this happens to someone and there is no doctor or medicine present, then he should immediately place his index finger on the mouth of the wound itself as we have described.
It should be tightly bound until the blood is constricted and flows only above the wound and on the artery. The finger should not be removed by cold water continuously until the blood coagulates, thickens, and stops. During this time, observe what may be needed for cauterization or medication.
The Second Chapter.
On Incisions, Slit Incisions, Venesection, and Wounds and the Like.
Khallaf said: We have mentioned in the first chapter every disease that can be treated with cauterization by fire and burning medicines, along with their causes and reasons, instruments, and forms of cautery. We arranged them as sections from the heel to the head.
And I will follow the same approach in this chapter so that it is easy for the student to attain what he seeks.
Before I begin with this, it is necessary for you to know, O sons, that this chapter contains more precious information than what is in the first chapter regarding cauterization.
And for this reason, it is necessary that the warning be stronger because the work in this chapter involves a lot of bloodletting from the blood upon which life depends when opening a vein or making an incision on a swelling or draining an abscess or treating a wound or extracting an arrow or cutting for a stone and similar procedures, all of which are accompanied by danger and fear, and often result in death.
I warn you against falling into what is doubtful. For different kinds of people will come to you in this profession with various illnesses; some of them are tired of their illness and find death easy.
Due to the severity of his illness and the length of his suffering, and because the disease has taken such a form that it indicates death, there are others who will offer you money in hope of recovery, though their disease is fatal. Therefore, you should not assist those who come to you with this kind of situation at all.
Let your caution be greater than your desire and eagerness, and do not proceed with anything unless you are certain of the knowledge about what will result in a desirable outcome. Use foresight and warning regarding all treatments to ensure safety for your patients.
For in that you will find assistance in acquiring praise, glory, remembrance, and commendation. May God grant you wisdom, my sons, and may He not deprive you of correctness and success, for that is in His hands; there is no god but He.
I have organized this chapter into sections as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, from the heel to the head, to make it easier for you to find what you seek, if God wills.
The First Section.
On the Treatment of Water That Accumulates in the Heads of Children.
This illness often occurs in children at birth if the midwife presses the child's head too roughly. It can also occur due to an unknown hidden condition.
I have not seen this condition in anyone except children, and all whom I have seen suffered a quicker approach to death. Therefore, I have seen fit to refrain from treating it. Indeed, I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and the head grows larger every day. The child could not even sit due to the size of his head, and the moisture increased until he died.
This moisture either accumulates between the skin and the bone, or beneath the bone on the membrane. If the moisture is between the skin and the bone and the swelling is small, it should be necessary to make a single incision in the middle of the head horizontally, about two fingers long, so that the moisture can drain out. This is what the scalpel looks like.
If the moisture is more abundant and the swelling is larger, make two intersecting incisions as shown in this figure:.
If the moisture is beneath the bone, its sign is that you will see the sutures of the head open on all sides, and when you squeeze it with your hand, the water descends inward. You should then make three incisions in the middle of the head as shown in this figure:.
After the incision, all the moisture should be removed. Then, close the cuts with bandages and dressings. Cover it from above with drinks and oil until the fifth day, then loosen the bindings and treat the wound with linen strips and ointments. Do not keep the head tightly bound; feed the patient dry food with little moisture.
Until the organ strengthens and heals. Another method for incision is to observe where the bone of the swelling and accumulation of water are most apparent, as it may be more in the back of the head, or in the front, or on the right, or on the left.
Cut where the tumor and fluid accumulation are apparent, and cut as much as you can, but be careful not to cut an artery, for if you do, bleeding may occur, causing the patient to die from that hemorrhage despite the expulsion of moisture.
الفرع الثاني.
Cut the two arteries behind the known ears called the temporal arteries.
When a person suffers from a sudden severe attack affecting the eyes or the chest, and medication fails to provide relief, then the most effective treatment is to cut these two arteries.
When you wish to cut them, shave the patient's head with a razor, then rub the area with a rough cloth to make the artery visible. Then tie the patient’s neck with the edge of their garment. Look for where the pulse beats; it is in the two lower positions behind the ears, which are rarely hidden except in some people.
Then mark them with ink, and cut them with a sharp scalpel down to the bone; the width of the cut should be about the breadth of the head. If you prefer, insert the scalpel underneath the artery and cut upwards, the length of the cut being approximately two closed fingers.
When the artery is cut, blood will gush out in pulsating spurts. If the artery does not become visible to the touch, estimate three finger breadths from the ear and mark it with ink, then cut down to the bone. It is important that...
The bleeding should continue for six watches (approximately six hours) on average, though it may be more or less depending on the patient's strength and fullness of the arteries. Then examine the wound; if any part of the peritoneum remains attached to the bone, cut it away.
