Until you are certain that nothing remains of the sac, then treat the wound with ointments until it heals. If the tumor contains fatty tissue, cut it open in this manner:.
Make an incision in a hardened area and place the forceps at the edges of the wound and peel it back on all sides, exerting your effort to remove the omentum that contains it. If an artery is encountered, do as described for you afterward. Do the same with the tumor if it is encased within the incision.
The treatment is exactly as I have mentioned, and incising a hardened tumor is easier because it has little blood and moisture. Some of these tumors in the head may have no moisture at all; for instance, I made an incision on a tumor that.
I incised a tumor on the head of an old woman and found the tumor hard like a stone, rough and white, so much so that it would not break even if someone threw it, which would injure them. None of the other tumors that occur in the heads of people, such as those that appear in the heads of children, are like this one.
At the origins of the ears, incise them completely with a simple cut and make the bottom part open so that the discharge can flow downward easily. Then treat it with appropriate remedies.
Chapter Forty-Two.
On Incising Tumors That Appear in the Neck. These tumors often appear in the neck, under the armpits, and in the armpit regions. They may also occur throughout the body. Those that appear in the neck are usually one or few and some of them develop from others.
Every sow of them is inside a special membrane as in abscesses and tumors of the head as we have described, and there are many types of these sows, some calcified, some containing moisture, and some foul and unresponsive to treatment.
I have not seen any of them in good condition to the touch; its appearance was close to the color of the skin, moving in all directions, and it was not adhered to the neck nerve or the thyroid cartilage nor a blood vessel, and it was not sunken. It is necessary to cut it with a simple incision from top to bottom of the body in this shape from line ~ج~ to line ~ب~:.
And peel it from all sides and stretch the edges of the skin with a single clamp or two clamps or many clamps if necessary, as we mentioned in tumors of the head. Remove it little by little and be careful not to cut any vein or nerve. The scalpel should not be extremely sharp.
So as not to overcut with your hand or disturb the patient by cutting what is not necessary. If you cut a vein or artery and it hinders your work, place powdered zinc or some small pieces that stop bleeding in the wound.
And close the wound and leave it until the inflammation subsides and the wound relaxes, indicating that it is about to become pus-filled. At this point, stop bleeding and return to your work until you finish. Then examine with your index finger if any smaller sows remain and cut them out and clean them.
If there is a large vein at the root of the pig’s tail, it should not be cut there. Instead, it should be tied tightly with a double thread until it falls off by itself without harm. Then stuff the wound with old cotton that has been dipped in Egyptian ointment and treat it.
If the entire pig's tail is cut, you should gather the edges of the wound and stitch it immediately after ensuring that no part remains. If you see that a piece of the pig’s tail bone remains.
You should aim to cut at the root and base, and use suturing as we have mentioned. For pigs that contain moisture, apply a simple bandage where you see evidence of healing, and make sure the bandage covers the lower part as we said.
Then, after the bandage, use linen strips dipped in Egyptian ointment or similar to consume any remaining corruption. When you see that the wound has cleansed itself, treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth until it heals.
Chapter Forty-Three.
On Incising the Throat for a Tumor Occurring Inside the Throat.
The earlier scholars mentioned this incision in the throat, but I have not seen anyone in our country perform it. This is their discourse. As for those with a condition (disease), they should avoid making an incision in the throat as it does not benefit them.
Because all the veins and the lung are diseased, and for those with a hot tumor in the mouth, throat, or tonsils, if there is no issue in the windpipe, it is necessary to use an incision in the throat to avoid the harm that can come from choking.
When we wish to do so, we should cut the throat below three or four circles of the trachea, a small incision in width between two circles, as much as the incision in the mesentery and not in the cartilage, and this place is suitable for the incision.
Because it has little flesh and the blood vessels are far from it, if the surgeon is timid, he should stretch the throat skin with a retractor, then cut the skin until he reaches the trachea; if he sees any blood vessels, he should avoid them.
Then he should incise the mesentery as described, and determine the incision of the trachea from the phlegm that comes out with each coughing and from the interruption of voice; leave the wound open for a time until the period in which choking was feared has passed, then bring together the edges of the wound with skin sutures.
And it is treated separately from the cartilage, then use medications that promote flesh growth until he recovers. The author of this book explains that the meaning of this statement we quoted is when they see the patient's throat blocked by one of these tumors which were mentioned.
And when the patient is near death and his life is in danger, they resort to cutting the throat so that the patient can breathe through the incision and be saved from death. They are instructed to leave the wound open until the period of illness subsides, and this period should last three days or so.
At that time, they were ordered to suture the wound and treat it until he recovers. What I witnessed myself was a servant who took a knife and made an incision on her throat, cutting part of her trachea. She was brought to me for treatment and appeared to be fainting as if slaughtered; upon examination, I opened the wound.
I found the blood that came out of the wound to be minimal, so I concluded that she had not cut an artery or a vein. The breath was coming out of the wound, so I quickly sutured the wound and treated it until it healed, and nothing happened to the servant except for hoarseness in her voice, no more.
She returned to her best condition after a few days. From this, we say that cutting the throat is not dangerous.
Chapter Forty-Four.
On incising the tumor that appears in the throat from the outside and is called the elephant of the throat.
This tumor called the elephant of the throat is a large swelling in the color of the body. It is common in women and there are two types of it.
It may be either natural or accidental. As for the natural one, there is no remedy for it. As for the accidental one, it is of two kinds: one resembles fatty tumors, and the other resembles a tumor that results from the entanglement of an artery, and there is danger in incising it. It should not be subjected to treatment with a blade at all, except for what is small. If you probe it and examine it carefully and find that it resembles a fatty tumor and is not connected to any arteries, then incise it as you would a fatty tumor. Remove it along with the capsule if it is within a capsule. If not, carefully extract all of it and then treat the area as necessary.
Chapter Forty-Five.
In the incision for various types of abscesses.
There are many types of abscesses, and I have mentioned all their kinds in the classification. Here, it is important to explain the difference between an abscess and a carbuncle, as this can be confusing. I say that a carbuncle is accompanied by heat, fever, and terrifying pains until the fermentation subsides. The pus completes its formation, and then the fever and intensity subside. An abscess does not come with heat, fever, or pain; it is contained within a specific serous cavity that matches the color of the body. It begins like a lentil and grows to resemble an egg, becoming larger or smaller.
There are two types of abscesses: one is fatty, and the other contains moisture, with various colors of moisture as mentioned in the classification. When you proceed to treat an abscess, you should first probe it and examine it with a tool called a medus, as its description will be shown in the subsequent section.
Assess the size of the swelling, then remove the medus and observe what comes out with it. If watery discharge of any color emerges, make a simple incision as described for other tumors. If no moisture comes out after using the medus, know that it is a fatty abscess.
Make a firm incision on it in the manner I have shown you, and hang it with clamps. Gently peel the skin away from all sides and, if possible, remove the serous cavity intact along with the abscess.
If the sac bursts during the procedure and you cannot remove it intact, this often happens; remove it piece by piece until nothing remains. For if any part of it remains, whether little or much, the condition will most likely recur.
If the condition overpowers you and only a small part remains, clean the wound thoroughly with sharp corroding agents when you finish, tighten the wound, place something above it that quiets the hot swelling, and treat it with all remedies until it heals. If the defect is large, outline its edges and treat it to promote healing.
If a troublesome or non-troublesome vein is encountered and bleeding occurs, immediately clean the area with powdered cautery and leave it compressed for two or three days until the wound begins to heal and the blood flow subsides. Then return to cutting what remains of the defect.

Chapter Forty-Seven.
On the Treatment of Male Breasts.
Some people’s breasts may become swollen at the onset of puberty to the point where they resemble women’s breasts, remaining as ugly swellings. For those who dislike this, it is advisable to make a crescent-shaped incision on the breast as shown in this illustration.
From line ~b~ to line ~c~:. Then remove all the fat, fill the wound with healing fatty medicine, and stitch the edges of the incision together. Treat it until it heals. If the breast sags downward and droops due to its bone structure as often happens in women.
It is advisable to make two incisions in the upper sides of the breast, resembling a crescent shape, connecting at their ends to form larger and smaller arcs around each other as shown in this illustration:. From line ~b~ to line ~c~, then remove the skin between the two incisions, extract the fat, and use the stitching and bandaging methods, along with any other necessary treatment, until it heals.
If you are unable to excise what should be excised due to the patient's anxiety or because of excessive bleeding, then you should pack the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment until it corrodes the remaining fat, and then treat it until it heals.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
On the treatment of tumors that appear under the armpit.
These tumors that appear under the armpit are of a type similar to pigs, solid and enclosed in a sac. Some contain moisture; those that do should be incised in a crescent shape as follows.
From line ~b~ to line ~c~. Once you have completely evacuated all the contents of the tumor over a period of time, pack it with old cotton and leave it for another day, then remove the cotton.
Treat it with the appropriate ointment until it heals. If the tumor is of the type of pig's nodules, incise it as described in the section on incision for pigs. If the wound persists and pus spreads, apply cauterization as previously mentioned.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
On incising a tumor that appears near an artery or vein, and it is called aneurysm.
If an artery is cut and the skin above it heals, a tumor often appears as a result. The same can also occur with a vein, where swelling and a tumor may appear.
And the signs by which it is known whether the tumor and swelling are from an artery or a vein: if the tumor is from an artery, it will be elongated and gathered deep in the body; and when you press on the tumor with your finger, you feel it as though it has a grating sound.
And if it is from a vein, the tumor will be round on the surface of the body; and cutting into these tumors is dangerous, especially those in the armpit, elbow, neck, and many other places in the body that are very large; therefore, treatment with iron should be avoided.
And those in the limbs or in the head should also be avoided; if it is an expansion at the mouth of an artery, then cut into the skin longitudinally, then open the incision with pincers, then peel away the artery and free it from the fasciae.
Until it is exposed, then insert a needle under it and pass it to the other side, then tie off the artery with a double thread in two places as I have described in tying off the arteries in the temples. Then cut between the ligatures until all the blood has come out.
And the swelling will resolve, then use treatments that promote suppuration until the ligatures fall off, then treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If the tumor is from cutting into a vein, then grasp as much of the tumor with the skin as possible with your hand, then insert a needle below where you are grasping and pass it through with a double thread until it emerges on the other side. Then tie the tumor tightly as I have told you about tying a grape from both sides with the ends of the thread. If you fear that the threads will slip, insert another needle with another thread under the entire tumor at the intersection of the first needle.
Tighten your threads at four places, then cut open the tumor in the middle until what is inside comes out, then cut off the excess skin but leave what was tied. Then place a dressing on it that has been soaked in syrup and oil. Then use the treatment that involves bandages and ointments until it heals.
Chapter Fifty.
On the tumor that results from nerve strain.
Just as a tumor can occur in an artery or vein, a tumor can also occur in a nerve if it is struck or due to excessive fatigue or similar causes. This is more common in the wrists and ankles.
And in every place where a joint moves, there is a wandering tumor that has the same color as the rest of the body. It is usually painless, but when pressed firmly, the patient feels a sensation like numbness. The tumor does not gather deeply within the flesh.
Rather, it is under the skin and moves in all directions but does not go forward or backward. If it occurs in the joints, it should not be treated with iron, as it may cause long-term issues. If it occurs on the head or forehead,
Cut the skin with a scalpel. If the tumor is small, grasp it with tweezers and cut it from its base. If it is large, attach it to a traction device, peel it off, then remove it and stitch the wound together, treating it until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-One.
On the Cutting of Warts That Appear on the Abdomen.
Warts, which are often found on people's abdomens and other parts of their bodies and are called fungal warts due to their resemblance to mushrooms, have a thin root and a thick head. They can split into two and grow from small ones to very large ones.
I once saw a man with two warts on his abdomen that most resembled mushrooms, white and thin at the root, having split into two parts and cracked, with moisture constantly seeping from them. I cut them out, and they weighed about eighteen ounces for one and six ounces for the other.
To perform the cutting, examine the patient. If the patient is moist and the wart is white, moist, and has a thin root, cut it with a wide scalpel. Have cautery irons ready in the fire because often a lot of blood flows when they are cut.
If the bleeding becomes overwhelming, apply cautery. If the patient is timid and frightened by cutting with iron, take a tight lead thread and tie it around the wart that has this description, then leave it for two days. Then tighten the lead thread more, continuing to do so.
Tighten the thread until it affects the wart so that it falls off on its own without further effort. If the wart has a thick root, there is some risk in cutting it, especially those found on the abdomen. However, it may be possible to cut half of it or part of it.
Then cauterize it so that it does not return, then treat it until the wound heals. Beware of exposing yourself to cutting a tumor that is pale in color, insensitive, and repulsive in appearance, for it is a cancerous swelling, and we will come to mention cancer after this.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
On the Treatment of Umbilical Hernia.
Umbilical hernia has many causes; either it results from the rupture of the abdominal fascia, through which the intestines or bowel protrude as in other hernias, or it is due to blood that emerges from a vein or artery, as previously mentioned, or it is caused by gas that accumulates inside.
If it is due to the rupture of the abdominal fascia and the protrusion of the intestines, then the color of the swelling will resemble the color of the body, it will be soft without pain, and its appearance will vary in position. If it is due to the protrusion of the bowel, its position will differ even more from what we have described; if you press on it with your fingers, it disappears and then returns, and there may be gurgling sounds. It also tends to enlarge significantly when taking a bath or after severe exertion. If it is due to moisture, it will be soft.
It does not disappear if you press it with your hand, nor does it increase or decrease. If it is due to blood, the swelling will appear dark alongside these signs. If it is due to a growth of flesh, the swelling will be raised and hard, and it will remain at a constant size.
If it is due to gas, touching it will be soft. The approach in such cases is to observe; if the umbilical hernia is caused by blood from an artery or vein, or by gas, you should refrain from treating it, as there is a risk and potential harm involved, as I informed you in the chapter that discusses tumors arising from arteries or veins.
If the umbilical hernia is towards the abdomen or the flank, you should order the patient to hold themselves and stand erect. Then apply a plaster around the entire navel. Then order him to lie down in front of you on his back. Then make a wide incision around the navel where you applied the plaster. Then push up the center of the swelling with a large forceps, then tightly tie off the area of the incision with strong thread or silk.
The knot of the ligature should be a slipknot. Then open the center of the constricted swelling above the ligature and insert your index finger to feel for the intestines. If you find that the intestines have been caught by the ligature, loosen the slipknot and push the intestines back into the abdomen. If you find a hernia, hold it with forceps.
Cut away the excess. If an artery or vein obstructs you, ligate it carefully and return to your work. Take two needles and thread them with strong threads, then insert the needles into the incision made around the swelling at four points where they have been passed through, then secure the swelling in four places with the needles.
If you wish, remove the needles and leave the area so that the constricted flesh rots and falls off on its own, or cut it when it has become thin and rotten. Then treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals. If the umbilical hernia consists of protruding flesh.
Or if it is due to moisture, you should incise the swelling as described and remove the blood or moisture that you find within. Then treat it with something that will heal the area.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
في علاج السرطان.
في التقسيم ذكرنا أنواع السرطان وكيفية علاجها بالأدوية، وتحذير من علاجه بالحديد لئلا يتقرح، وذكرنا أيضا السرطان المتولد في الرحم والتحذير من علاجه.
وذكرت الأوائل أنه متى كان السرطان في موضع يمكن استئصاله كله، مثل السرطان الذي يكون في الثدي أو في الفخذ ونحوها من الأعضاء المتمكنة لإخراجه بجملته، ولا سيما إذا كان مبتدئاً صغيراً. وأمّا متى قدم وكان عظيماً فلا ينبغي أن تقربه.
فعندما استطعت لم أبرئ منه أحداً، ولا رأيت قبلى غيري يصل إلى ذلك. والعمل فيه إذا كان متمكنا كما قلنا أن تتقدم فتسهل من المررة السوداء مرارا ثم تفصده إن كان في العروق امتلاء بيّن.
ثم تنصب المريض نصبة يتمكن فيها من العمل، ثم تلقى في السرطان الصنانير التي تصلح له، ثم تقوره من كل جهة مع الجلد على استقصاء حتى لا يبقى شيء من أصوله، واترك الدم يجري ولا تقطعه سريعا.
بل اعصر المواضع وأسلت الدم الغليظ كله بيديك أو بما أمكنك من الآلات. فإن اعترضك في العمل نزف دمعظيم من قطع شريان أو وريد فاكو العرق حتى ينقطع الدم، ثم عالجه بسائر العلاج إلى أن يبرأ.
Chapter Forty-Four.
On the Treatment of Hemorrhoids.
In the classification, we have informed about the types of dropsy, how water accumulates in each type, the signs of each type, and their treatment with medicines. The type that is treated with iron is solely the zaki (visceral) type; the tabbi (peripheral) type and the lahani (fleshy) type are never approached with iron at all.
If that is the case, it is fatal; if you have treated this zaki type of hemorrhoids with medicines and your treatment has not been successful, then examine whether the patient is extremely weak or suffers from another illness in addition to the hemorrhoids, such as.
cough or diarrhea, and the like; then beware of treating him with iron, for it is dangerous. If you see that the patient is strong, has no other illness besides hemorrhoids alone, and is neither a child nor an elderly person, then the approach to treatment should be to have the patient stand before you. And have a servant stand behind him to squeeze his abdomen with his hands and push the water downward towards the pubic region. Then take a sharp instrument in this manner:.
long and defined at both ends like a scalpel, except that it is slightly blunt so as not to pierce too deeply into the intestines during the procedure and cause harm. Then observe; if the hemorrhoids have developed from the side of the intestines.
You should make an incision three fingerbreadths below the navel, above the pubic region. If the hemorrhoids have developed due to liver disease, your incision should be three fingerbreadths to the left of the navel. If they have developed due to spleen disease, your incision should be three fingerbreadths to the right side.
Also, it should not be incised on the side on which the patient wishes to lie down so that the exudate does not flow to that weak area. Then puncture the skin completely with the instrument, then insert the instrument into this incision and raise your hand.
With the scalpel, between the skin and subcutaneous tissue as if you were peeling it, and the amount you peel should be about the size of a fingernail or similar. Then puncture the serosa until the scalpel reaches an empty space, which is where the fluid is, then remove it and insert into this hole the instrument which looks like this.
It is similar to a tube made of thin reed, crafted from silver or copper or polished sheet metal. At the bottom, it has a small hole, and on its sides, there are three holes: two on one side and one on another side as you can see.
And its end may be sharpened like that of a pen, as shown in this illustration:.
At the top of it is a ring. When the instrument reaches the fluid, it will flow onto the instrument immediately. Therefore, let an adequate amount of fluid be drained over time because if you drain more than what is appropriate at once, the patient may die due to the dissolution of their vital spirit.
Or he may become unconscious, nearly dying. However, drain from him according to his strength, as indicated by the patient's condition, such as the strength of his pulse and the improvement in his color. Then remove the instrument and stop draining the fluid, for it will be stopped immediately.
Because of the skin that holds the hole in the serosa which you were told to seal as described, then reinsert the instrument another day if you see that the patient can tolerate it.
Also, a small amount of water is removed; you do this for several days while keeping the neck [or part in question] dry and being careful not to make a mistake so that only a little water remains. If you are concerned about the patient and leave a large amount of water, then treat it by burying it in hot sand.
Excessive sweating in the bath and sun, keeping him thirsty, and treating him with drying medicines until he recovers, and cauterize the stomach, liver, and spleen after removing the water as described above.
Chapter Fifty-five.
On the treatment of children who are born with the urethral opening not pierced or with a narrow or misplaced opening.
Some boys may be born with their urethra not pierced, so it is necessary to pierce it as soon as they are born.
With a very thin scalpel, as shown in this illustration:.
Then place a thin lead pin in the hole and secure it for three or four days. When he needs to urinate, move it aside, then put it back afterward. If you do not use the lead, the urine passing through that area may prevent it from closing up.
As for those whose urethral opening is narrow, it should be treated with lead as we have said for many days until it widens. Those whose urethra is in the wrong place are also treated: some are born with the opening at the end of the urethra and thus cannot urinate forward.
Until he raises the urethra with his hand upwards, and it should not protrude before him because semen cannot reach the uterus straight, which is a very ugly defect, and the reason for this work is that the patient lies on his back.
Then stretch his urethra with your left hand strongly, and shave the tip of the urethra with a sharp blade like a penknife or as if you were carving something to make it protrude like a ball so that the hole is in the center as required.
Be cautious during your work about bleeding, as it often occurs, so counteract it with something that stops the blood and treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Six
On the abscess that occurs in the bladder, urethra, blackish area, corruption, and adhesion of the bladder to the urethra.
This abscess often occurs in the urethra, it is a fleshy swelling and can be either malignant or non-malignant. The non-malignant one should be attached with a delicate fishhook.
Cut it until you cleanse it completely, then apply a cotton swab soaked in Egyptian ointment, and afterward treat it with palm ointment until it heals. However, if the abscess is malignant and dark-colored, cauterization should be used after cutting and exposing it.
If the abscess is in the foreskin of a person who has not been circumcised, and part of the abscess is inside the foreskin while part is outside, then you should first remove the part of the abscess that is inside until it heals, and then treat the external part.
For when you treat them together, you cannot be sure that the tunica vaginalis will not rupture. It may also happen in the testicles and in the tunica vaginalis that they turn black and become diseased; therefore, it is necessary to excise all that has turned black or is about to decay or has already decayed.
Then apply honey mixed with ground and sieved pomegranate peels and wormwood. Then treat it with all other treatments until it heals. If bleeding occurs, use cauterization with a crescent-shaped cautery as shown in this figure:.
For cauterization is beneficial for both conditions, namely bleeding and a diseased wound. If the tunica vaginalis atrophies and disappears altogether at some point, it is necessary to insert a lead tube into the urethra so that the patient can urinate through it. As for the adherence of the tunica vaginalis to the testicle:
This adherence occurs in those whose tunica vaginalis is intact and who have not undergone circumcision. It may also occur due to a wound or swelling. Therefore, it is necessary to peel it off with a thin scalpel until the ligament loosens and the testicle is freed from all sides.
If it is difficult to distinguish them during examination, then peel off some of the testicle and tunica vaginalis. The tunica vaginalis is thin and may rupture quickly due to its thinness. Then separate the tunica vaginalis from the testicle with a fine linen strip moistened in cold water so that they do not adhere as well.
Then treat it with a styptic drink until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Seven.
في طهارة الصبيان وعلاج ما يعرض لهم من الخطر.
الختان ليس بشيء غير تفريق الإتصال كسائر الجراحات إلا أنه لكونه من عملنا بإرادتنا واستعماله في الصبيان خاصة وجب أن نرسم فيه العمل الأفضل.
وال طريق الأسهل المؤدي إلى السلامة، فأقول إنّ الأوائل لم تذكر الختان في شيء من كتبها لأنّه لم يكن يستعمل في شرائعهم وإنما هو ما اكتسبناه.
بالتجربة وذلك أنى وجدت الجمهور من الصناع والحجامين يستعملون التطهير بالموس وبالمقص ويفعلون الفكة والربط بالخيط والقطع بالظفر وقد جربت جميع هذه الوجوه.
فلم أجد أفضل من التطهير بالمقص والربط بالخيط لأن التطهير بالموس كثيرا ما تلوذ له الجلدة لأنه جلدة الغلفة طبقتان فربما قطعت الجلدة العليا وبقيت الطبقة السفلى.
فيضطر إلى قطع آخر وألم مستأنف والتطهير بالفكة لا يؤمن معها قطع طرف الإحليل لأنّه ربما دخل في ثقبها، وأمّا التطهير بالظفر فربما فلت الجلدة وفسد عملك أو كانت جلدة الصبي قصيرة بالطبع..
فكثيرا ما يولدون كذلك لا يحتاجون إلى تطهير وقد رأيت ذلك، وأمّا التطهير بالمقص والربط بالخيط فالتجربة كشفت لي فضله لأن المقص متناسقة القطع من أجل أن الشفرة التي من فوق كالشفرة التي من أسفل.
When you press your hand with the proper alignment of the blades, you will make a single measurement and cut in one time without error at all; the stitch should be like a wall around the bladder's skin from every side. The first step is to instruct the boy.
Especially if he is one who understands a little that you are only tying the thread in his bladder and leave it for another day, then cheer him up and please him with every face you can make and what his mind accepts, then have him stand before you upright.
He must not be sitting, and hide the scissors in your sleeve or under your foot so that the boy's eye does not fall on them at all, nor on any of the instruments. Then insert your hand into his bladder and blow into the skin and lift it up until the tip of the bladder comes out.
Then clean it from what accumulates in it of dirt. Then tie the marked place with a folded thread, then tie another one a little below it. Then grasp with your thumb and index finger the lower tying spot well and cut between the two ties. Then lift the skin up quickly and pull out the tip of the bladder, then let the blood flow a little as it is better and causes less swelling of the bladder. Then dry it with a wet cloth, then sprinkle it with dried and burned gourd ash, which is the best I have tried, or flour of barley, which is also excellent.
